<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="2.2.-FULL-Joins">2.2. FULL Joins<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.-FULL-Joins">&#182;</a></h3><ul>
<li>The last of the three types of OUTER Joins is the FULL Join</li>
<li>Explore the difference between FULL Join and other Joins<ul>
<li>The instruction will focus on comparing them to Inner Joins and LEFT Joins and then to LEFT Joins and RIGHT Joins.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Let's review how the diagram changes between and Inner Join and a LEFT Join for our bAsic example Using the left and right tables.</li>
<li>Then we'll delve into the FULL Join diagram and is SQL code. </li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/join.png", height="200", width="100" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><ul>
<li>Recall that an Inner Join keeps only the records that have matching key field values in both tables.
<br>
<br>
<br>
<br>
<br></li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/left_join.png", height="200", width="100" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><ul>
<li>A LEFT Join keeps all of the records in the left table while bringing in missing values for those key field values that don't appear in the right table.</li>
</ul>
<p><br>
<br>
<br>
<br>
<br></p>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/right_join.png", height="200", width="100" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><ul>
<li>Let's review the differences between a LEFT Join and a RIGHT Join.</li>
<li>The id values of 2 and 3 in the left table do not match with the id values in the right table, so missing values are brought in for them in the LEFT Join. </li>
<li>Likewise for the RIGHT Join, missing values are brought in for id values of 5 and 6.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>A <strong>FULL Join</strong> combines a LEFT Join and RIGHT Join As you can see in the diagram.</li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/full_join.png", height="400", width="200" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><p><p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> left_table.id <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> L_id, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> right_table.id <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> R_id, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> left_table.val, <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> L_val, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> right_table.val <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> R_val <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> left_table <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Full Join </span> right_table <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (id);
</p></p>
<ul>
<li>It will bring in all record From both the left and the right table and keep track of the missing values accordingly.</li>
<li>Note the missing values here and all six of the values of id are included in the table.</li>
<li>You can also see From the SQL code, to produce this FULL Join result, the general format aligns closely with the SQL syntax seen for an Inner Join and a LEFT Join.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="2.2.1.-FULL-Join-example-using-leaders-database">2.2.1. FULL Join example using leaders database<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.1.-FULL-Join-example-using-leaders-database">&#182;</a></h4><ul>
<li>Let's revisit the example of looking at countries with prime ministers and / or presidents.</li>
<li>Query breakdown:<ul>
<li>The Select statement includes the country field From both tables of interest and also the prime_minister and president fields.</li>
<li>The left table is specified As prime_ministers with the aliAs of p1</li>
<li>The order matters and if you switched the two tables, the output would be slightly different.</li>
<li>The right table is specified As presidents with the aliAs of p2</li>
<li>The Join is done bAsed on the key field of country in both tables</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> p1.country <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> pm_co, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> p2.country <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> pres_co, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> prime_minister, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> president, <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> prime_ministers <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p1 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Full Join </span> presidents <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p2 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> p1.country=p2.country;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[83]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select p1.country As pm_co,</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    p2.country As pres_co, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    prime_minister, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    president </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.prime_ministers As p1 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">FULL Join leaders.presidents As p2 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ON p1.country = p2.country;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h4 id="2.2.2.-Exercises">2.2.2. Exercises<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.2.-Exercises">&#182;</a></h4>
</div>
</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="2.2.2.1.-FULL-Join">2.2.2.1. FULL Join<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.2.1.-FULL-Join">&#182;</a></h5><p>In this exercise, you'll examine how your results differ when Using a full Join versus Using a left Join versus Using an Inner Join with the <code>countries</code> and <code>currencies</code> tables.</p>
<p>You will focus on the North American <code>region</code> and also where the <code>name</code> of the country is missing. Dig in to see what we mean!</p>
<p>Begin with a full Join with <code>countries</code> on the left and <code>currencies</code> on the right. The fields of interest have been <code>Select</code>ed for you throughout this exercise.</p>
<p>Then complete a similar left Join and conclude with an Inner Join.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Choose records in which region corresponds to North America or is NULL.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> code, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> region, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> basic_unit
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From to countries </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to to currencies </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Full Join </span> currencies <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where region is North America or null </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> region='North America' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or</span> region <span style="color:#FF0000";> Is Null </span> <br>;
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> region;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[84]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select name As country, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    code, region, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    basic_unit </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">FULL Join countries.currencies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where region = &#39;North America&#39; OR region Is Null </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY region;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>

<table border="1" class="dataframe">

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Have you kept an eye out on the different numbers of records these queries returned? The <code>FULL Join</code> query returned 17 rows, the <code>LEFT Join</code> returned 4 rows, and the <code>Inner Join</code> only returned 3 rows. Do these results make sense to you?</strong></p>

</div>
</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="2.2.2.3.-FULL-Join-(2)">2.2.2.3. FULL Join (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.2.3.-FULL-Join-(2)">&#182;</a></h5><p>You'll now investigate a similar exercise to the last one, but this time focused on Using a table with more records on the left than the right. You'll work with the <code>languages</code> and <code>countries</code> tables.
Begin with a full Join with <code>languages</code> on the left and <code>countries</code> on the right. Appropriate fields have been Selected for you again here.
<strong>Instructions 1/3</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Choose records in which <code>countries.name</code> starts with the capital letter <code>'V'</code> or is <code>NULL</code> and arrange by <code>countries.name</code> in <strong>Ascending</strong> order to more clearly see the results.<p>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
  <span style="margin-left:3em"> code, <br>
  <span style="margin-left:3em"> languages.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From languages </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to to countries </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Inner Join </span> countries <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where region countries.name starts with V or is null </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'V%' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Is Null </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> countries.name;
</p></li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[87]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select countries.name, code, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    languages.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">FULL Join countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where countries.name LIKE &#39;V</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">&#39; OR countries.name IS null </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY countries.name; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Repeat the same query As above but use a <code>left Join</code> instead of a full Join. Note what hAs changed compared to the full Join result!</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> code, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> languages.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From languages </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to to countries </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Left Join </span> countries <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where countries.name starts with V or is null </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'V%' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Is Null </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> countries.name;
</p>

<span class="s2">                languages.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 3)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Repeat once more, but use an <code>Inner Join</code> instead of a left Join. Note what hAs changed compared to the full Join and left Join results.<p>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
  <span style="margin-left:3em"> code, <br>
  <span style="margin-left:3em"> languages.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From languages </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to countries </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Inner Join </span> countries <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
  <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where countries.name starts with V or is null </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'V%' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or </span> countries.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Is Null </span> <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> countries.name;
</p></li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[89]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select countries.name, code, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                languages.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where countries.name Like &#39;V</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">&#39; OR countries.name IS null </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY countries.name;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="2.2.2.3.-FULL-Join-(3)">2.2.2.3. FULL Join (3)<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.2.3.-FULL-Join-(3)">&#182;</a></h5><p>You'll now explore Using two consecutive full Joins on the three tables you worked with in the previous two exercises.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Complete a full Join with <code>countries</code> on the left and <code>languages</code> on the right.</li>
<li>Next, full Join this result with <code>currencies</code> on the right.</li>
<li>Use <code>LIKE</code> to choose the Melanesia and Micronesia regions (Hint: <code>'M%esia'</code>).</li>
<li>Select the fields corresponding to the country name <code>As country</code>, region, language name <code>As language</code>, and basic and fractional units of currency.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> c1.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> region, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> l.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> basic_unit, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> frac_unit <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From countries (alias as c1) </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c1 <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to languages </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Full Join </span> languages <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> l <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to currencies (alias as c1) </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Full Join </span> currencies <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c2 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Using </span> (code) <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where region like Melanesia and Micronesia </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> region <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'M%esia';
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[90]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select c1.name As country, region, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    l.name As language, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    basic_unit, frac_unit </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries As c1 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">FULL Join countries.languages As l </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">FULL Join countries.currencies As c2 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where region Like &#39;M</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">esia&#39;;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="2.2.2.4-Review-OUTER-Joins">2.2.2.4 Review OUTER Joins<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.2.4-Review-OUTER-Joins">&#182;</a></h5><p>A(n) <code> ___ </code> Join is a Join combining the results of a <code> ___ </code> Join and a <code> ___ </code> Join.
<strong>Answer the question</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><del>left, full, right</del></li>
<li><del>right, full, left</del></li>
<li><del>Inner, left, right</del></li>
<li><strong><strong>None of the above are true</strong>&lt;/strong&gt;</li>
</ol>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="2.3.-Cross-join">2.3. Cross-join<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.3.-Cross-join">&#182;</a></h3><p>CROSS Joins create all possible combinations of two tables.</p>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/cross_join.png", height="400", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><ul>
<li>The resulting table is comprised of all 9 combinations if <code>id</code> From <code>table1</code> and <code>id</code> From <code>table2</code> (e.g. 1(A-C), 2(A-C), &amp; 3(A-C))</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="2.3.1.-CROSS-Join-example:-Pairing-prime-ministers-with-presidents">2.3.1. CROSS Join example: Pairing prime ministers with presidents<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.3.1.-CROSS-Join-example:-Pairing-prime-ministers-with-presidents">&#182;</a></h4><ul>
<li>Suppose all prime ministers in North America and Oceania in the <code>prime_ministers</code> table are scheduled for individual meetings with all presidents in the presidents table.</li>
<li>All the combinations can be created with a CROSS Join</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> prime_minister, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> president, <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> prime_ministers <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p1 <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to languages </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Cross Join </span> presidents <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p2 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> p1.continent <span style="color:#FF0000";> In </span> ('North America', 'Oceania');
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[91]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select prime_minister, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    president </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.prime_ministers As p1 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">CROSS Join leaders.presidents As p2 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where p1.continent IN (&#39;North America&#39;, &#39;Oceania&#39;);&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h5 id="2.3.1.1.-Exercises">2.3.1.1. Exercises<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.3.1.1.-Exercises">&#182;</a></h5>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>A table of two cities</strong></p>
<p>This exercise looks to explore languages potentially and most frequently spoken in the cities of Hyderabad, India and Hyderabad, Pakistan.</p>
<p>You will begin with a cross Join with <code>cities As c</code> on the left and <code>languages As l</code> on the right. Then you will modify the query Using an Inner Join in the next tab.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Create the cross Join As described above. (Recall that cross Joins do <strong>not</strong> use <code>ON</code> or <code>Using</code>.)</li>
<li>Make use of <code>LIKE</code> and <code>Hyder%</code> to choose Hyderabad in both countries.</li>
<li>Select only the city name <code>As city</code> and language name <code>As language</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> c.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> city, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> l.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> cities <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Cross Join </span> languages <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> l <br>
        <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> c.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'Hyder%';
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[94]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select c.name As city, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                l.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities As c </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">CROSS Join countries.languages As l </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where c.name Like &#39;Hyder</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">&#39;;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">unique_lang</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">hyderabad_lang</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="s1">&#39;language&#39;</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">unique</span><span class="p">()</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">len</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">unique_lang</span><span class="p">))</span>
<span class="n">hyderabad_lang</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">hyderabad_lang</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<p>Use an Inner Join instead of a cross Join. Think about what the difference will be in the results for this Inner Join result and the one for the cross Join.</p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> c.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> city, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> l.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> language <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> cities <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Inner Join </span> languages <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> l <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> c.country_code=l.code <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> c.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> 'Hyder%';
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[95]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select c.name As city, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                l.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities As c </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.languages As l </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On c.country_code = l.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where c.name LIKE &#39;Hyder</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">&#39;;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Outer challenge</strong></p>
<p>Now that you're fully equipped to use outer Joins, try a challenge problem to test your knowledge!
In terms of life expectancy for 2010, determine the names of the lowest five countries and their regions.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Select country name <code>As country</code>, <code>region</code>, and life expectancy <code>As life_exp</code>.</li>
<li>Make sure to use <code>LEFT Join</code>, <code>Where</code>, <code>Order BY</code>, and <code>LIMIT</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> c.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> country, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> c.region, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> p.life_expectancy <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> life_exp <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Left Join </span> populations <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> c.code=l.country_code <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> p.year=2010 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> life_exp
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Limit </span> 5;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[96]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;Select c.name As country, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    c.region, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                    p.life_expectancy As life_exp </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries As c </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT Join countries.populations As p </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On c.code = p.country_code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where p.year = 2010 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY life_exp </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Limit 5;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h2 id="3.-Set-theory-clauses">3. Set theory clauses<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.-Set-theory-clauses">&#182;</a></h2><p>In this chapter, you'll learn more about set theory Using Venn diagrams and you will be introduced to union, union all, intersect, and except clauses. You'll finish by investigating semi-Joins and anti-Joins, which provide a nice introduction to subqueries.</p>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/ven.jpg", height="350", width="400" /></center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="3.1.-State-of-the-UNION">3.1. State of the UNION<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.-State-of-the-UNION">&#182;</a></h3><ul>
<li>Focus on the operations UNION and UNION ALL.</li>
<li>In addition to Joining diagrams, you'll see how Venn diagrams can be used to represent set operations.</li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/uni_alluni.png", height="350", width="400" /></center><ul>
<li>Think of each circle As representing a table of data</li>
<li><p>The shading represents what's included in the result of the set operation From each table.</p>
</li>
<li><p><strong><code>UNION</code></strong> includes every record in both tables, but <strong>DOES NOT</strong> double count those that are in both tables.</p>
</li>
<li><strong><code>UNION ALL</code></strong> includes every record in both tables and <strong>DOES</strong> replicate those that are in both tables, represented by the black center</li>
<li>The two diagrams on the bottom represent only the subsets of data being Selected.</li>
<li><strong><code>INTERSECT</code></strong> results in only those records found in both of the tables.</li>
<li><strong><code>EXCEPT</code></strong> results in only those records in one table, <strong>BUT NOT</strong> the other.</li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/uni.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/uni_all.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><p><code>UNION</code> does have no duplicate while <code>UNION ALL</code> includes all duplicates.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="3.1.1.-UNION-&amp;-UNION-ALL-example">3.1.1. UNION &amp; UNION ALL example<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.1.-UNION-&amp;-UNION-ALL-example">&#182;</a></h4><p><code>monarchs</code> table in the <code>leaders</code> databAse
Use <code>UNION</code> on the <code>prime_ministers</code> and <code>monarchs</code> tables
all prime ministers and monarchs</p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> prime_minister <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> leader, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> UNION </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> monarch, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.monarchs <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> country;
</p><ul>
<li>Note that the <code>prime_minister</code> field hAs been aliAsed As leader. The resulting field from the <code>UNION</code> will have the name <strong>leader</strong>.<ul>
<li>This is an important property of <em>set theory</em> clauses</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The fields included in the operation must be of the same data type since they are returned As a single field.<ul>
<li>A number field can't be stacked on top of a character field.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Spain and Norway have a prime minister and a monarch, while Brunei and Oman have a monarch who also acts As a prime minister.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> prime_minister <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> leader, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> UNION ALL </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> monarch, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.monarchs <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> country;
</p><ul>
<li><code>UNION</code> and <code>UNION ALL</code> clauses do not do the lookup step that <code>Join</code>s do, they stack records on top of each other From one table to the next.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">

<span class="s2">From leaders.monarchs;&quot;</span>

<h4 id="3.1.2.-Exercises">3.1.2. Exercises<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.2.-Exercises">&#182;</a></h4>

<h5 id="3.1.2.1.-UNION">3.1.2.1. UNION<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.2.1.-UNION">&#182;</a></h5><p>Near <strong>query result</strong> to the right, you will see two new tables with names <code>economies2010</code> and <code>economies2015</code>.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Combine these two tables into one table containing all of the fields in <code>economies2010</code>. The <code>economies</code> table is also included for reference.</li>
<li>Sort this resulting single table by country code and then by year, both in Ascending order.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> * <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.economies2010 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> UNION </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> * <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.economies2015 <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> code, year;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[100]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select * </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.economies2010 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    UNION </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select * </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.economies2015 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY code, year; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<h5 id="3.1.2.2.-UNION-(2)">3.1.2.2. UNION (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.2.2.-UNION-(2)">&#182;</a></h5><p><code>UNION</code> can also be used to determine all occurrences of a field across multiple tables. Try out this exercise with no starter code.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Determine all (non-duplicated) country codes in either the <code>cities</code> or the <code>currencies</code> table. The result should be a table with only one field called <code>country_code</code>.</li>
<li>Sort by <code>country_code</code> in alphabetical order.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country_code <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.citie <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> UNION </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> code <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.currencies <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> country_code;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[101]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select country_code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">UNION </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.currencies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY country_code;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">country_codes</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="n">country_codes</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>

<h5 id="3.1.2.3.-UNION-ALL">3.1.2.3. UNION ALL<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.2.3.-UNION-ALL">&#182;</a></h5><p>As you saw, duplicates were removed From the previous two exercises by Using <code>UNION</code>.
To include duplicates, you can use <code>UNION ALL</code>.</p>
<Strong>Instructions</Strong><ul>
<li>Determine all combinations (include duplicates) of country code and year that exist in either the <code>economies</code> or the <code>populations</code> tables. Order by <code>code</code> then <code>year</code>.</li>
<li>The result of the query should only have two columns/fields. Think about how many records this query should result in.</li>
<li>You'll use code very similar to this in your next exercise after the video. Make note of this code after completing it.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> code, year <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.economies <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> UNION All</span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country_code, year <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.populations <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> code, year;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[103]:</div>

<span class="s2">Select code, year </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.economies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    UNION ALL </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select country_code, year </span><span class="se">\</span>

<span class="s2">ORDER BY code, year; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<h3 id="3.2.-INTERSECT">3.2. INTERSECT<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.2.-INTERSECT">&#182;</a></h3><p><center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/intersect.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center></p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> id <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> left_one <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Intersect </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> id <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> right_one;
</p><ul>
<li><p>The set theory clause <strong><code>INTERSECT</code></strong> works in a similar fAshion to <code>UNION</code> and <code>UNION ALL</code>, but remember From the Venn diagram, <code>INTERSECT</code> only includes those records in common to both tables and fields Selected.</p>
</li>
<li><p>The result only includes records common to the tables Selected</p>
</li>
<li>Determine countries with both a prime minister and president</li>
<li>The code for each of these set operations has a similar layout.<ul>
<li>First Select which fields to include From the first table, and then specify the name of the first table.</li>
<li>Specify the set operation to perform</li>
<li>Lastly, denote which fields to include From the second table, and then the name of the second table.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Intersect </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.presidents;
</p><p><strong>What happens if two columns are Selected, instead of one?</strong></p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> prime_minister <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> leader <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Intersect </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> country, president <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.presidents;
</p><ul>
<li>Will this also give you the names of the countries with both type of leaders?</li>
<li>This results in an empty table.</li>
<li>When <code>INTERSECT</code> looks at two columns, it includes both columns in the search.<ul>
<li>It didn't find any countries with prime ministers <strong>AND</strong> presidents having the same name.</li>
<li><code>INTERSECT</code> looks for <strong>records</strong> in common, not individual key fields like what a Join does to match.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[105]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select country </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.prime_ministers </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">INTERSECT </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select country </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.presidents </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries.populations <br>

</p>

<h5 id="3.2.1.2.-INTERSECT-(2)">3.2.1.2. INTERSECT (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.2.1.2.-INTERSECT-(2)">&#182;</a></h5><p>As you think about major world cities and their corresponding country, you may Ask <em>which countries also have a city with the same name As their country name</em>?</p>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="3.2.1.3.-Review-UNION-and-INTERSECT">3.2.1.3. Review UNION and INTERSECT<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.2.1.3.-Review-UNION-and-INTERSECT">&#182;</a></h5><p>Which of the following combinations of terms and definitions is correct?</p>
<p><strong>Answer the question</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><del>UNION: returns all records (potentially duplicates) in both tables</del></li>
<li><del>UNION ALL: returns only unique records</del></li>
<li><strong><strong>INTERSECT: returns only records appearing in both tables</strong>&lt;/strong&gt;</li>
<li><del>None of the above are matched correctly</del></li>
</ol>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="3.3.-EXCEPT">3.3. EXCEPT<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.3.-EXCEPT">&#182;</a></h3><center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/except.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> monarch, country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.monarchs <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Intersect </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> prime_minister, country <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers;
</p><ul>
<li><strong><code>EXCEPT</code></strong> includes only the records in one table, but not in the other.</li>
<li><p>There are some monarchs that also act As the prime minister.  One way to determine those monarchs in the monarchs table that do not also hold the title prime minister, is to use the <code>EXCEPT</code> clause.</p>
</li>
<li><p>This SQL query Selects the monarch field From monarchs, then looks for common entries with the prime_ministers field, while also keeping track of the country for each leader.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Only the two European monarchs are not also prime ministers in the leaders database.</p>
</li>
<li><p>Only the records that appear in the left table, <strong>BUT DO NOT</strong> appear in the right table are included.</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[108]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">

<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<h5 id="3.3.1.1.-EXCEPT">3.3.1.1. EXCEPT<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.3.1.1.-EXCEPT">&#182;</a></h5><p>Get the names of cities in <code>cities</code> which are not noted As capital cities in <code>countries</code> As a single field result.</p>
<p>Note that there are some countries in the world that are not included in the <code>countries</code> table, which will result in some cities not being labeled As capital cities when in fact they are.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Order the resulting field in Ascending order.</li>
<li>Can you spot the city/cities that are actually capital cities which this query misses?</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[109]:</div>

<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    EXCEPT </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select capital </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY name; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>

<h5 id="3.3.1.2.-EXCEPT-(2)">3.3.1.2. EXCEPT (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.3.1.2.-EXCEPT-(2)">&#182;</a></h5><p>Now you will complete the previous query in reverse!</p>

<li>The <code>cities</code> table contains information about 236 of the world's most populous cities. The result of your query may surprise you in terms of the number of capital cities that DO NOT appear in this list!</li>
</ul>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="3.4.-Semi-Joins-and-Anti-Joins">3.4. Semi-Joins and Anti-Joins<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.-Semi-Joins-and-Anti-Joins">&#182;</a></h3><ul>
<li>The previous six Joins are all additive Joins, in that they add columns to the original left table.<ul>
<li>Inner Join</li>
<li>SELF Join</li>
<li>LEFT Join</li>
<li>RIGHT Join</li>
<li>FULL Join</li>
<li>CROSS Join</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p>The lAst two Joins use a right table to determine which records to keep in the left table.</p>
<ul>
<li>Use these lAst to Joins in a way similar to a WHERE clause dependent on the values of a second table.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p><code>semi-Joins</code> and <code>anti-Joins</code> don't have the same built-in SQL syntax that Inner Join and LEFT Join have.</p>
</li>
<li><code>semi-Joins</code> and <code>anti-Joins</code> are useful tools in filtering table records on the records of another table.</li>
<li>The challenge will be to combine set theory clauses with semi-Joins.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="3.4.1.-SEMI-Join">3.4.1. SEMI Join<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.1.-SEMI-Join">&#182;</a></h4><ul>
<li>Determine the presidents of countries that gained independence before 1800.<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/semi_join.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center></li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> president, country, continent <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.presidents <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> country <span style="color:#FF0000";>In </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select </span> name <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.states <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> indep_year&lt1800);
</p><p>This is an example of a subquery, which is a query that sits inside another query.</p>
<ul>
<li><p>Does this include the presidents of Spain and Portugal?</p>
<ul>
<li>Since Spain does not have a president, it's not included here and only the Portuguese president is listed.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p>The <code>semi-Join</code> chooses records in the first table where a condition <strong>IS</strong> met in the second table.</p>
</li>
<li>The <code>semi-Join</code> matches records by key field in the right table with those in the left.</li>
<li>It then picks out only the rows in the left table that match the condition.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[111]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select president, country, continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.presidents </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE country IN </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    (Select name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     WHERE indep_year &lt; 1800); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[111]:</div>



<div class="output_html rendered_html output_subarea output_execute_result">

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="3.4.2.-ANTI-Join">3.4.2. ANTI Join<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.2.-ANTI-Join">&#182;</a></h4><ul>
<li>Determine countries in the AmericAs founded after 1800.</li>
</ul>
<center><img src="/assets/images/sql1/anti_join.png", height="300", width="150" style="float: left; margin-right: 10px; margin-bottom: 5px" /></center><p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> president, country, continent <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.presidents <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> continent <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> '%America' <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> And </span> country <span style="color:#FF0000";> Not In </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select </span> name <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.states <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> indep_year&lt1800);
</p><ul>
<li>An <code>anti-Join</code> chooses records in the first table where a condition <strong>IS NOT</strong> met in the second table.</li>
<li>Use <code>NOT</code> to exclude those countries in the subquery.</li>
<li>The <code>anti-Join</code> picks out those columns in the left table that do not match the condition on the right table.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[112]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select president, country, continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.presidents </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE continent LIKE &#39;</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">America&#39; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    AND country NOT IN </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        (Select name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         WHERE indep_year &lt; 1800); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h5 id="3.4.3.1.-Semi-Join">3.4.3.1. Semi-Join<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.3.1.-Semi-Join">&#182;</a></h5><p>You are now going to use the concept of a semi-Join to identify languages spoken in the Middle East.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Flash back to our <a href="https://www.datacamp.com/courses/intro-to-sql-for-data-science">Intro to SQL for Data Science</a> course and begin by Selecting all country codes in the Middle EAst As a single field result Using <code>Select</code>, <code>From</code>, and <code>Where</code>.</li>
</ul>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>You are now going to use the concept of a semi-Join to identify languages spoken in the Middle East.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Comment out the answer to the previous tab by surrounding it in <code>/*</code> and <code>*/</code>. You'll come back to it!</li>
<li>Below the commented code, Select only unique languages by name appearing in the <code>languages</code> table.</li>
<li>Order the resulting single field table by <code>name</code> in Ascending order.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>

<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY name; </span><span class="se">\</span>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>You are now going to use the concept of a semi-Join to identify languages spoken in the Middle East.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 3)</strong></p>
<p>Now combine the previous two queries into one query:</p>
<ul>
<li>Add a <code>Where In</code> statement to the <code>Select Distinct</code> query, and use the commented out query From the first instruction in there. That way, you can determine the unique languages spoken in the Middle EAst.</li>
</ul>
<p>Carefully review this result and its code after completing it. It serves As a great example of subqueries, which are the focus of Chapter 4.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[118]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where code In </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2"> (Select code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  Where region = &#39;Middle East&#39;) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY name; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="3.4.3.2.-Relating-semi-Join-to-a-tweaked-Inner-Join&lt;">3.4.3.2. Relating semi-Join to a tweaked Inner Join&lt;<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.3.2.-Relating-semi-Join-to-a-tweaked-Inner-Join&lt;">&#182;</a></h5><p>Let's revisit the code From the previous exercise, which retrieves languages spoken in the Middle East.</p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select Distinct</span> name <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> code <span style="color:#FF0000";> In </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select </span> name <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> region='Middle East') <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> name;
</p><p>Sometimes problems solved with semi-Joins can also be solved Using an Inner Join.</p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select Distinct</span> languages.name <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span>  language <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Inner Join </span> countries <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> languages.code = countries.code <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> region='Middle East') <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> language;
</p><p>This Inner Join isn't quite right. What is missing From this second code block to get it to match with the correct answer produced by the first block?</p>
<p><strong>Possible Answers</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><del><code>HAVING</code> instead of <code>WHERE</code></del></li>
<li><strong><strong><code>DISTINCT</code></strong>&lt;/strong&gt;</li>
<li><del><code>UNIQUE</code></del></li>
</ol>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[120]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT languages.name As language </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On languages.code = countries.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where region = &#39;Middle East&#39; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY language;&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h5 id="3.4.3.3.-Diagnosing-problems-Using-anti-Join">3.4.3.3. Diagnosing problems Using anti-Join<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.3.3.-Diagnosing-problems-Using-anti-Join">&#182;</a></h5><p>Another powerful Join in SQL is the anti-Join. It is particularly useful in identifying which records are caUsing an incorrect number of records to appear in Join queries.</p>
<p>You will also see another example of a subquery here, As you saw in the first exercise on semi-Joins. Your goal is to identify the currencies used in Oceanian countries!</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Begin by determining the number of countries in <code>countries</code> that are listed in Oceania Using <code>Select</code>, <code>From</code>, and <code>WHERE</code>.</li>
</ul>

</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">

<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select count(name) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where continent = &#39;Oceania&#39;; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>

<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Complete an Inner Join with <code>countries As c1</code> on the left and <code>currencies As c2</code> on the right to get the different currencies used in the countries of Oceania.</li>
<li>Match <code>ON</code> the <code>code</code> field in the two tables.</li>
<li>Include the country <code>code</code>, country <code>name</code>, and <code>bAsic_unit As currency</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Observe query result and make note of how many different countries are listed here.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[122]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select c1.code, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        c1.name, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        c2.bAsic_unit As currency </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries As c1 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.currencies As c2 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On c1.code = c2.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where continent = &#39;Oceania&#39;; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 3)</strong></p>
<p>Note that not all countries in Oceania were listed in the resulting Inner Join with currencies. Use an anti-Join to determine which countries were not included!</p>
<ul>
<li>Use <code>NOT IN</code> and <code>(Select code From currencies)</code> As a subquery to get the country code and country name for the Oceanian countries that are not included in the <code>currencies</code> table.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[123]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select code, name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  WHERE continent = &#39;Oceania&#39; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    AND code NOT IN </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    (Select code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From countries.currencies); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<h5 id="3.4.3.4.-Set-theory-challenge">3.4.3.4. Set theory challenge<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.4.3.4.-Set-theory-challenge">&#182;</a></h5><p>Congratulations! You've now made your way to the challenge problem for this third chapter. Your tAsk here will be to incorporate two of <code>UNION</code>/<code>UNION ALL</code>/<code>INTERSECT</code>/<code>EXCEPT</code> to solve a challenge involving three tables.</p>
<p>In addition, you will use a subquery As you have in the lAst two exercises! This will be great practice As you hop into subqueries more in Chapter 4!</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Identify the country codes that are included in either <code>economies</code> or <code>currencies</code> but not in <code>populations</code>.</li>
<li>Use that result to determine the names of cities in the countries that match the specification in the previous instruction.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[125]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select country_code, name </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities As c1 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where country_code In </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    (Select e.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From countries.economies As e </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     UNION ALL </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     Select c2.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From countries.currencies As c2 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     EXCEPT </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     Select p.country_code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From countries.populations As p); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

<h2 id="4.-Subqueries">4. Subqueries<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.-Subqueries">&#182;</a></h2><p>In this closing chapter, you'll learn how to use nested queries to add some finesse to your data insights. You'll also wrap all of the content covered throughout this course into solving three challenge problems.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="4.1.-Subqueries-inside-WHERE-and-Select-clauses">4.1. Subqueries inside WHERE and Select clauses<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.1.-Subqueries-inside-WHERE-and-Select-clauses">&#182;</a></h3><ul>
<li>The most common type of subquery is one inside of a <code>WHERE</code> statement.<ul>
<li>Examples include semi-Join and anti-Join</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[126]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name, fert_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where continent = &#39;Asia&#39; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">And fert_rate &lt;  </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">(Select AVG(fert_rate) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2"> From leaders.states); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[126]:</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<ul>
<li>The second most common type of subquery is inside of a <code>Select</code> clause.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Count the number of countries listed in states table for each continent in the <code>prime_ministers</code> table.</strong></p>
<p><strong>Continents in the <code>prime_ministers</code> table</strong></p>
<p><strong>Determine the counts of the number of countries in states for each of the continents in the lAst slide</strong></p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select count</span>(name)<br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.states <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> continent <span style="color:#FF0000";> In </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select Distinct</span> continent <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers); <br>
<span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From languages </span> <br>
</p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select Distinct</span> continent, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select Count</span>(*) <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.states <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> prime_ministers.continent = states.continent) <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> countries_num <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> leaders.prime_ministers;
</p><ul>
<li>The subquery involving states, can also reference the <code>prime_ministers</code> table in the main query.</li>
<li>Anytime you do a subquery inside a <code>Select</code> statement, you need to give the subquery an aliAs (e.g. <code>countries_num</code> in the example)</li>
<li>There are numerous ways to solve problems with SQL queries.
A carefully constructed Join could achieve this same result.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[127]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT continent, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">            (Select COUNT(*) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">             From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">             Where prime_ministers.continent = states.continent) As countries_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.prime_ministers </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h4 id="4.1.1.-Exercises">4.1.1. Exercises<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.1.1.-Exercises">&#182;</a></h4>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="4.1.1.1.-Subquery-inside-WHERE">4.1.1.1. Subquery inside WHERE<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.1.1.1.-Subquery-inside-WHERE">&#182;</a></h5><p>You'll now try to figure out which countries had high average life expectancies (at the country level) in 2015.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Begin by calculating the average life expectancy across all countries for 2015.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[128]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select avg(life_expectancy) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.populations </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where year = 2015; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Recall that you can use SQL to do calculations for you. Suppose we wanted only records that were above <code>1.15 * 100</code> in terms of life expectancy for 2015:<p>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> *, <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> populations <br>
  <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> life_expectancy>1.15*100 <span style="color:#FF0000";> And </span> year=2015;
</p></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>Select all fields From <code>populations</code> with records corresponding to larger than 1.15 times the average you calculated in the first tAsk for 2015. In other words, change the <code>100</code> in the example above with a subquery.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[132]:</div>

    <div class="input_area">

<span class="s2">Select * </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.populations </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where life_expectancy &gt; 1.15 * </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">           (Select avg(life_expectancy) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">           From countries.populations </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">           Where year = 2015) And year = 2015; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>
