</div>
</div>

</div>

</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="4.1.1.2.-Subquery-inside-WHERE-(2)">4.1.1.2. Subquery inside WHERE (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.1.1.2.-Subquery-inside-WHERE-(2)">&#182;</a></h5><p>Use your knowledge of subqueries in <code>Where</code> to get the urban area population for only capital cities.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Make use of the <code>capital</code> field in the <code>countries</code> table in your subquery.</li>
<li>Select the city name, country code, and urban area population fields.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[130]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name, country_code, urbanarea_pop </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where name In </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  (Select capital </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">   From countries.countries) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY urbanarea_pop Desc; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<h5 id="4.1.1.3-Subquery-inside-Select">4.1.1.3 Subquery inside Select<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.1.1.3-Subquery-inside-Select">&#182;</a></h5><p>In this exercise, you'll see how some queries can be written Using either a Join or a subquery.</p>
<p>You have seen previously how to use <code>GROUP BY</code> with aggregate functions and an Inner Join to get summarized information From multiple tables.</p>
<p>The code given in <strong>query.sql</strong> Selects the top nine countries in terms of number of cities appearing in the <code>cities</code> table. Recall that this corresponds to the most populous cities in the world. Your tAsk will be to convert the commented out code to get the same result As the code shown.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<p>Submit your Answer:</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[131]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select countries.name As country, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        COUNT(*) As cities_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On countries.code = cities.country_code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Group BY country </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY cities_num Desc, country </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">LIMIT 9; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>

<li>Convert the <code>GROUP BY</code> code to use a subquery inside of <code>Select</code>, i.e. fill in the blanks to get a result that matches the one given Using the <code>GROUP BY</code> code in the first query.</li>
<li>Again, sort the result by <code>cities_num</code> descending and then by <code>country</code> Ascending.</li>
</ul>

<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select countries.name As country, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      (Select count(*) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       Where countries.code = cities.country_code) As cities_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY cities_num Desc, country </span><span class="se">\</span>

<h3 id="4.2.-Subquery-inside-From-clause">4.2. Subquery inside From clause<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.-Subquery-inside-From-clause">&#182;</a></h3><p>The last basic type of subquery exists inside of a <code>From</code> clause. <strong>Determine the maximum percentage of women in parliament for each continent listing in <code>leaders.states</code></strong></p>
<p>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> continent, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Max</span>(women_parli_perc) <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> max_perc <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> states <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Group By </span> continent <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> continent;
</p><ul>
<li>This query will only work if <code>continent</code> is included As one of th fields in the <code>Select</code> clause, since we are grouping bAsed on that field.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[134]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select continent, MAX(women_parli_perc) As max_perc </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Group BY continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY continent; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<p><strong>FocUsing on records in monarchs</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><p>Multiple tables can be included in the <code>From</code> clause, by adding a comma between them</p>
</li>
<li><p>Produces part of the answer; how should duplicates be removed?</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[135]:</div>

    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select monarchs.continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.monarchs, leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where monarchs.continent = states.continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY continent; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Finishing the subquery</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><p>To get Asia and Europe to appear only once, use <code>DISTINCT</code> in the <code>Select</code> statement.</p>
</li>
<li><p>How is the <code>max_perc</code> column included with continent?
Instead of including states in the <code>From</code> clause, include the subquery instead and aliAs it with a name like <code>subquery</code>.</p>
</li>
<li><p>This is how to include a subquery As a temporary table in the <code>From</code> clause.</p>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[136]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT monarchs.continent, subquery.max_perc </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From leaders.monarchs, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    (Select continent, MAX(women_parli_perc) As max_perc </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     From leaders.states </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">     GROUP BY continent) As subquery </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">WHere monarchs.continent = subquery.continent </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY continent; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[136]:</div>

<h4 id="4.2.1.-Exercises">4.2.1. Exercises<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.1.-Exercises">&#182;</a></h4>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="4.2.1.1.-Subquery-inside-From">4.2.1.1. Subquery inside From<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.1.1.-Subquery-inside-From">&#182;</a></h5><p>The last type of subquery you will work with is one inside of <code>From</code>.</p>
<p>You will use this to determine the number of languages spoken for each country, identified by the country's local name! (Note this may be different than the <code>name</code> field and is stored in the <code>local_name</code> field.)</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<p>Begin by determining for each country code how many languages are listed in the <code>languages</code> table using <code>Select</code>, <code>From</code>, and <code>GROUP BY</code>.
Alias the aggregated field As <code>lang_num</code>.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[137]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select code, count(name) As lang_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY lang_num DESC; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">lang_count</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lang_count</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">())</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lang_count</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">tail</span><span class="p">())</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt"></div>


<div class="output_subarea output_stream output_stdout output_text">

    code  lang_num

</pre>
</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Include the previous query (aliAsed As <code>subquery</code>) As a subquery in the <code>From</code> clause of a new query.</li>
<li>Select the local name of the country From <code>countries</code>.</li>
<li>Also, Select <code>lang_num</code> From <code>subquery</code>.</li>
<li>Make sure to use <code>WHERE</code> appropriately to match <code>code</code> in <code>countries</code> and in <code>subquery</code>.</li>
<li>Sort by <code>lang_num</code> in descending order.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[139]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select local_name, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        subquery.lang_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        (Select code, count(name) As lang_num </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         From countries.languages </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         Group BY code) As subquery </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         Where countries.code = subquery.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY lang_num DESC; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">lang_count</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lang_count</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">())</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lang_count</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">tail</span><span class="p">())</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output">

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h5 id="4.2.1.2.-Advanced-subquery">4.2.1.2. Advanced subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.1.2.-Advanced-subquery">&#182;</a></h5><p>You can also nest multiple subqueries to answer even more specific questions.
In this exercise, for each of the six continents listed in 2015, you'll identify which country had the maximum inflation rate (and how high it was) Using multiple subqueries. The table result of your query in <strong>Task 3</strong> should look something like the following, where anything between <code>&lt;</code> <code>&gt;</code> will be filled in with appropriate values:</p>
<table>
<thead><tr>
<th style="text-align:center">name</th>
<th style="text-align:center">continent</th>
<th style="text-align:center">inflation_rate</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country1&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">North America</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation1&gt;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country2&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Africa</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation2&gt;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country3&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Oceania</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation3&gt;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country4&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Europe</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation4&gt;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country5&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">South America</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation5&gt;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;country6&gt;</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Asia</td>
<td style="text-align:center">&lt;max_inflation6&gt;</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/pre&gt;
Again, there are multiple ways to get to this solution Using only Joins, but the focus here is on showing you an introduction into advanced subqueries.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions 1)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Create an Inner Join with <code>countries</code> on the left and <code>economies</code> on the right with <code>Using</code>. Do not alias your tables or columns.</li>
<li>Retrieve the country name, continent, and inflation rate for 2015.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[140]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name, continent, inflation_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    Inner Join countries.economies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE year = 2015; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">inf_rate</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">inf_rate</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">())</span>
<span class="nb">print</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">inf_rate</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">tail</span><span class="p">())</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt"></div>


<div class="output_subarea output_stream output_stdout output_text">

0           Afghanistan           Asia          -1.549
1                Angola         Africa          10.287
2               Albania         Europe           1.896
3  United Arab Emirates           Asia           4.070
4             Argentina  South America             NaN
             name continent  inflation_rate
180         Samoa   Oceania           1.923

184      Zimbabwe    Africa          -2.410
</pre>
</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 2)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Determine the maximum inflation rate for each continent in 2015 Using the previous query As a subquery called <code>subquery</code> in the <code>From</code> clause.</li>
<li>Select the maximum inflation rate <code>As max_inf</code> grouped by continent.</li>
<li>This will result in the six maximum inflation rates in 2015 for the six continents as one field table. (Don't include <code>continent</code> in the outer <code>Select</code> statement.)</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[141]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select max(inflation_rate) As max_inf </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From ( </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      Select name, continent, inflation_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      Inner Join countries.economies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      Using (code) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">      WHERE year = 2015) As subquery </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY continent; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[141]:</div>

    </tr>
    <tr>
      <th>5</th>
      <td>9.784</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
</div>
</div>

</div>

</div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p><strong>Instructions 3)</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Append the second part's query to the first part's query using <code>Where</code>, <code>And</code>, and <code>In</code> to obtain the name of the country, its continent, and the maximum inflation rate for each continent in 2015. Revisit the sample output in the Assignment text at the beginning of the exercise to see how this matches up.</li>
<li>For the sake of practice, change all Joining conditions to use <code>On</code> instead of <code>Using</code>.</li>
<li>This code works since each of the six maximum inflation rate values occur only once in the 2015 data. Think about whether this particular code involving subqueries would work in cAses where there are ties for the maximum inflation rate values.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[142]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name, continent, inflation_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    Inner Join countries.economies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    ON countries.code = economies.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">  WHERE year = 2015 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">    AND inflation_rate IN ( </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         Select max(inflation_rate) As max_inf </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">         From ( </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">               Select name, continent, inflation_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">               From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">               Inner Join countries.economies </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">               ON countries.code = economies.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">               WHERE year = 2015) As subquery </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">        GROUP BY continent); </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>

<h5 id="4.2.1.3.-Subquery-challenge">4.2.1.3. Subquery challenge<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.1.3.-Subquery-challenge">&#182;</a></h5><p>Let's test your understanding of the subqueries with a challenge problem! Use a subquery to get 2015 economic data for countries that do not have</p>
<ul>
<li><code>gov_form</code> of <code>'Constitutional Monarchy'</code> or</li>
<li><code>'Republic'</code> in their <code>gov_form</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>Here, <code>gov_form</code> stands for the form of the government for each country. Review the different entries for <code>gov_form</code> in the <code>countries</code> table.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Select the country code, inflation rate, and unemployment rate.</li>
<li>Order by inflation rate Ascending.</li>
<li>Do not use table aliAsing in this exercise.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Select fields </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> code, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> inflation_rate, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> unemployment_rate <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From economies </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> economies <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where year is 2015 and code is not in </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> year=2015 <span style="color:#FF0000";> And </span> code <span style="color:#FF0000";> Not In </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Subquery of the codes that gov_form is 'Constitutional Monarchy' or '%Republic' </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:4em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select</span> code <br>
    <span style="margin-left:4em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <br>
    <span style="margin-left:4em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> (gov_form='Constitutional Monarchy' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or </span> gov_form <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> '%Republic'))<br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Order by inflation rate </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> inflation_rate;
</p>
</div>

<h5 id="4.2.1.4.-Subquery-review">4.2.1.4. Subquery review<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.2.1.4.-Subquery-review">&#182;</a></h5><p>Within which SQL clause are subqueries most frequently found?</p>
<p><strong>Answer the question</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><strong><strong>Where</strong>&lt;/strong&gt;</li>
<li><del>From</del></li>
<li><del>Select</del></li>
<li><del>IN</del></li>
</ol>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="4.3.-Course-Review">4.3. Course Review<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.3.-Course-Review">&#182;</a></h3><ul>
<li>In SQL, a Join combines columns From one or more tables in a relational databAse via a lookup process.</li>
<li>There are four types of Joins covered in this course</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Types of Joins:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li><p>Inner Join: also denoted As Join</p>
<ul>
<li>Self-Joins: special cAse</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p>OUTER Join</p>
<ul>
<li>LEFT Join: also denoted As LEFT OUTER Join</li>
<li>RIGHT Join: also denoted As RIGHT OUTER Join</li>
<li>FULL Join: also denoted As FULL OUTER Join</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><p>CROSS Join: create all possible combinations between two tables</p>
</li>
<li>Semi-Join / Anti-Join</li>
</ol>
<blockquote><p><strong>Notes</strong></p>
<ul>
<li><p>Words appearing in ALL capital letters correspond to Joins having simple SQL syntax.
Self-Joins, semi-Joins, and anti-Joins don't have built-in SQL syntax.</p>
</li>
<li><p>An Inner Join keeps only the records in which the key field (or fields) is in both tables.
A LEFT Join keeps all the records in fields specified in the left table and includes the matches in the right table bAsed on the key field or fields.
Key field values that don't match in the right table are included As missing data in the resulting table of a LEFT Join.</p>
</li>
<li><p>A RIGHT Join keeps all the records specified in the right table and includes the matches From the key field(s) in the left table.
THose that don't match are included As missing values in the resulting table From the RIGHT Join query.</p>
</li>
<li><p>A FULL Join is a combination of a LEFT Join and a RIGHT Join showing exactly which values appear in both tables and those that appear in only one or the other table.
A CROSS Join matches all records From fields specified in one table with all records From fields specified in another table.
Remember that a <code>CROSS Join</code> does not have an <code>On</code> or <code>Using</code> clause, but otherwise looks very similar to the code for an <code>Inner Join</code>, <code>LEFT Join</code>, <code>RIGHT Join</code>, or <code>FULL Join</code>.</p>
</li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<p><strong>Set Theory Clauses</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Recall that <code>UNION</code> includes every record in both tables but <strong>DOES NOT</strong> double count those that are in both tables.</li>
<li><code>UNION ALL</code> <strong>does</strong> replicate those that are in both tables.</li>
<li><code>INTERSECT</code> gives only those records found in both of the two tables.</li>
<li><code>EXCEPT</code> gives only those records in one table <strong>but not</strong> the other.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Semi-Joins and Anti-Joins</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>When you'd like to filter your first table bAsed on conditions set on a second table, you should use a semi-Join to accomplish the tAsk.</li>
<li>If instead you'd like to filter the first table bAsed on conditions <strong>NOT</strong> being met on a second table, you should use an anti-Join.<ul>
<li>Anti-Joins are particularly useful in diagnosing problems with other Joins in terms of getting fewer or more records than expected.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Types of basic subqueries</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The most common type of subquery is done inside of a <code>WHERE</code> clause.</li>
<li>The next most frequent types of subqueries are inside <code>Select</code> clauses and inside <code>From</code> clauses.</li>
<li>Subqueries can also find their way into the ON statement of a Join in ways similar to what you've seen inside <code>WHERE</code> clauses too.</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="4.3.1.-Final-Challenge">4.3.1. Final Challenge<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.3.1.-Final-Challenge">&#182;</a></h4><p>Welcome to the end of the course! The next three exercises will test your knowledge of the content covered in this course and apply many of the ideAs you've seen to difficult problems. Good luck!</p>
<p>Read carefully over the instructions and solve them step-by-step, thinking about how the different clauses work together.
In this exercise, you'll need to <strong>get the country names and other 2015 data</strong> in the <code>economies</code> table and the <code>countries</code> table for <strong>Central American countries with an official language</strong>.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Select unique country names. Also Select the total investment and imports fields.</li>
<li>Use a left Join with <code>countries</code> on the left. (An Inner Join would also work, but pleAse use a left Join here.)</li>
<li>Match on <code>code</code> in the two tables <code>And</code> use a subquery inside of <code>On</code> to choose the appropriate <code>languages</code> records.</li>
<li><code>Order</code> by country name ascending.</li>
<li>Use table aliAsing but not field aliAsing in this exercise.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Select fields </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select Distinct </span> c.name, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:7em"> e.total_investment, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:7em"> e.imports <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From countries (with alias as c) </span> <br>
        <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to economies (with alias as e </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Left Join </span> economies <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> e <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Match on code in (c,e) and the c.code in official languages </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> (c.code=e.code<br>
    <span style="margin-left:4em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";>And</span> c.code <span style="color:#FF0000";>In</span> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select</span> l.code<br>
    <span style="margin-left:11em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> languages <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> l <br>
    <span style="margin-left:11em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> official='true'))<br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where region and year are correct</span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> year=2015 <span style="color:#FF0000";> And </span> region='Central America' <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Order by field</span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> name;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[144]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select DISTINCT c.name, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                e.total_investment, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                e.imports </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.countries As c </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT Join countries.economies As e </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">On (c.code = e.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                And c.code IN (Select l.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                              From countries.languages As l </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                              Where official = &#39;true&#39;))</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where year = 2015 And region = &#39;Central America&#39; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY name; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[144]:</div>



<div class="output_html rendered_html output_subarea output_execute_result">

<h4 id="4.3.2.-Final-Challenge-(2)">4.3.2. Final Challenge (2)<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.3.2.-Final-Challenge-(2)">&#182;</a></h4><p>Let's ease up a bit and calculate the average fertility rate for each region in 2015.</p>
<p><strong>Instructions</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Include the name of region, its continent, and average fertility rate aliAsed As <code>avg_fert_rate</code>.</li>
<li>Sort bAsed on <code>avg_fert_rate</code> ascending.</li>
<li>Remember that you'll need to <code>Group BY</code> all fields that aren't included in the aggregate function of <code>Select</code>.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Select fields </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> c.name, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:4em"> c.continent, <br>
        <span style="margin-left:4em"> Avg(p.fertility_rate) <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> avg_fert_rate <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From populations (with alias as p) </span> <br>
        <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> populations <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> p <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Join to countries (with alias as c </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Inner Join </span> countries <span style="color:#FF0000";> As </span> c <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Match on code in (p,c) </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> On </span> p.country_code=c.code<br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> year=2015<br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Group by continent and region </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Group By </span> c.continent, c.region <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Order by avg of fertility_rate </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> avg_fert_rate;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[145]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select c.region, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       c.continent, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       AVG(p.fertility_rate) As avg_fert_rate </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.populations As p </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Inner Join countries.countries As c </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">ON p.country_code = c.code </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where year = 2015 </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Group BY c.continent, c.region </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY avg_fert_rate; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<h4 id="4.3.3.-Final-Challenge-(3)">4.3.3. Final Challenge (3)<a class="anchor-link" href="#4.3.3.-Final-Challenge-(3)">&#182;</a></h4><p>Welcome to the lAst challenge problem. Remember that these challenges are designed to take you to the limit to solidify your SQL knowledge! Take a deep breath and solve this step-by-step.</p>
<p>You are now tAsked with determining the top 10 capital cities in Europe and the AmericAs in terms of a calculated percentage using <code>city_proper_pop</code> and <code>metroarea_pop</code> in <code>cities</code>.
Do not use table aliAsing in this exercise.</p>
<p><strong> Instructions </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Select the city name, country code, city proper population, and metro area population.</li>
<li>Calculate the percentage of metro area population composed of city proper population for each city in <code>cities</code>, aliased as <code>city_perc</code>.</li>
<li>Focus only on capital cities in Europe and the Americas in a subquery.</li>
<li>Make sure to exclude records with missing data on metro area population.</li>
<li>Order the result by <code>city_perc</code> descending.</li>
<li>Then determine the top 10 capital cities in Europe and the Americas in terms of this <code>city_perc</code> percentage.</li>
</ul>
<p>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Select fields </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Select </span> name, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> country_code, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> city_proper_pop, <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> metroarea_pop, <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Calculate city_perc </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:3em"> city_proper_pop/metroarea_pop*100 <span style="color:#FF0000";>As </span> city_perc<br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- From cities </span> <br>
        <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> cities <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Where the names from continent='Europe' or '%America' and metroarea_pop is not null</span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> name <span style="color:#FF0000";> In </span> <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> (<span style="color:#FF0000";>Select </span> capital <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> From </span> countries <br>
    <span style="margin-left:5em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> Where </span> (continent='Europe' <span style="color:#FF0000";> Or </span> continent <span style="color:#FF0000";> Like </span> '%America'))<br>
    <span style="margin-left:10em"> <span style="color:#FF0000";> And </span> metroarea_pop <span style="color:#FF0000";> Is Not Null </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#b0c4de";> -- Order by city_perc in descreasing order </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Order By </span> city_perc <span style="color:#FF0000";> Desc </span> <br>
    <span style="color:#FF0000";> Limit </span>10;
</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[146]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;</span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Select name, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       country_code, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       city_proper_pop, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       metroarea_pop, </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">       city_proper_pop / metroarea_pop * 100 As city_perc </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">From countries.cities </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Where name In </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">            (Select capital </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">             From countries.countries </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">             Where (continent = &#39;Europe&#39; OR continent Like &#39;</span><span class="si">%%</span><span class="s2">America&#39;)) </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">                       And metroarea_pop IS NOT NULL </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Order BY city_perc desc </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">Limit 10; </span><span class="se">\</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;</span>

<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<p><strong>Course Description</strong></p>
<p>The European Soccer Database contains data about 12,800 matches from 11 countries played between 2011-2015! Throughout this course, you will be shown filtered versions of the tables in this database in order to better explore their contents.</p>
<p>You’ve learned how to Joining Data in SQL from tables</p>
<ul>
<li>This course will teach you to wrangle, filter, and categorize information in a relational database.</li>
<li>Learn the robust use of CASE statements, subqueries, and window functions</li>
<li>By discovering some interesting facts about soccer using the European Soccer Database.</li>
</ul>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h2 id="1.-CASE-Statement">1. CASE Statement<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.-CASE-Statement">&#182;</a></h2><p>Learn how to use the <code>CASE WHEN</code> statement to create categorical variables, aggregate data into a single column with multiple filtering conditions, and calculate counts and percentages.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="1.1.-Basic-CASE-Usage">1.1. Basic CASE Usage<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.1.-Basic-CASE-Usage">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong> CASE Statement Introduction </strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Contains a <code>WHEN</code>, <code>THEN</code>, and <code>ELSE</code> statement, finished with <code>END</code>.<ul>
<li>Using <code>AND</code> to add multiple logical conditions to your <code>WHEN</code> clause.</li>
<li>If there is no <code>ELSE</code>, those don’t meet the conditions are NULL</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>CASE</code> statements are great for…<ul>
<li>Categorizing data</li>
<li>Filtering data with WHERE</li>
<li>Aggregating data</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>CASE</code> statements will return any value you specify in your <code>THEN</code> clause.<ul>
<li>This is an incredibly powerful tool for robust calculations and data manipulation when used in conjunction with an aggregate statement.</li>
<li>One key task you can perform is using <code>CASE</code> inside an <code>AVG</code> function to calculate a percentage of information in your database.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="1.1.1.-Example:-Basic-CASE-Statement">1.1.1. Example: Basic <code>CASE</code> Statement<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.1.1.-Example:-Basic-CASE-Statement">&#182;</a></h4><p>In this exercise, you will identify matches played between FC Schalke 04 and FC Bayern Munich.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[56]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;-- Identify the home team as Bayern Munich, Schalke 04, or neither</span>
<span class="s2">SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    CASE WHEN home_team_api_id = 10189 THEN &#39;FC Schalke 04&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">         WHEN home_team_api_id = 9823 THEN &#39;FC Bayern Munich&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">         ELSE &#39;Other&#39; END AS home_team,</span>
<span class="s2">    COUNT(id) AS total_matches</span>
<span class="s2">FROM Match</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE country_id = 7809 -- Germany</span>
<span class="s2">-- Group by the CASE statement alias</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY home_team;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[56]:</div>

<h3 id="1.2.-Complex-CASE-Statement">1.2. Complex <code>CASE</code> Statement<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.2.-Complex-CASE-Statement">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong>CASE</strong> &amp; <strong>Alias</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Remember, just like subqueries, you don’t need alias statement inside <code>WHERE</code>.</li>
<li>But you need alias statement inside <code>SELECT</code>, <code>FROM</code>.</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="1.2.1.-Example:-CASE-Statements-Inside-SELECT,-Comparing-Column-Values">1.2.1. Example: <code>CASE</code> Statements Inside <code>SELECT</code>, Comparing Column Values<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.2.1.-Example:-CASE-Statements-Inside-SELECT,-Comparing-Column-Values">&#182;</a></h4><p>Barcelona is considered one of the strongest teams in Spain's soccer league.</p>
<p>You will be creating a list of matches in the 2011/2012 season where Barcelona was the "home team". You will do this using a CASE statement that compares the values of two columns to create a new group -- wins, losses, and ties.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[57]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT</span>
<span class="s2">    m.date,</span>
<span class="s2">    t.team_long_name AS opponent,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Complete the CASE statement with an alias</span>
<span class="s2">    CASE WHEN m.home_team_goal &gt; m.away_team_goal THEN &#39;Barcelona win!&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">        WHEN m.home_team_goal &lt; m.away_team_goal THEN &#39;Barcelona loss :(&#39; </span>
<span class="s2">        ELSE &#39;Tie&#39; END AS outcome </span>
<span class="s2">FROM Match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN Team AS t </span>
<span class="s2">ON m.away_team_api_id = t.team_api_id</span>
<span class="s2">-- Filter for Barcelona as the home team</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE m.home_team_api_id = 8634</span>
<span class="s2">  AND season = &#39;2011/2012&#39;;&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output">

<p>Now, construct a query to determine the outcome of Barcelona's matches where they played as the "away team".
 Did their performance differ from the matches where they were the home team?</p>

</div>

</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[58]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;-- Select matches where Barcelona was the away team</span>
<span class="s2">SELECT  </span>
<span class="s2">    m.date,</span>
<span class="s2">    t.team_long_name AS opponent,</span>
<span class="s2">    CASE WHEN m.home_team_goal &lt; m.away_team_goal THEN &#39;Barcelona win!&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">        WHEN m.home_team_goal &gt; m.away_team_goal THEN &#39;Barcelona loss :(&#39; </span>
<span class="s2">        ELSE &#39;Tie&#39; END AS outcome</span>
<span class="s2">FROM Match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">-- Join teams_spain to matches_spain</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN Team AS t </span>
<span class="s2">ON m.home_team_api_id = t.team_api_id</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE m.away_team_api_id = 8634</span>
<span class="s2">  AND season = &#39;2011/2012&#39;;&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h4 id="1.2.2.-Example:-Filtering-with-CASE-Statement-Inside-WHERE">1.2.2. Example: Filtering with <code>CASE</code> Statement Inside <code>WHERE</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#1.2.2.-Example:-Filtering-with-CASE-Statement-Inside-WHERE">&#182;</a></h4><p>Generate a list of matches won by Italy's Bologna team!</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[59]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;-- Select the season, date, home_goal, and away_goal columns</span>
<span class="s2">SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    season,</span>
<span class="s2">    date,</span>
<span class="s2">    home_team_goal,</span>
<span class="s2">    away_team_goal</span>
<span class="s2">FROM Match</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE </span>
<span class="s2">-- Exclude games not won by Bologna</span>
<span class="s2">    CASE WHEN home_team_api_id = 9857 AND home_team_goal &gt; away_team_goal THEN &#39;Bologna Win&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">        WHEN away_team_api_id = 9857 AND away_team_goal &gt; home_team_goal THEN &#39;Bologna Win&#39; </span>
<span class="s2">        END IS NOT NULL;&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>

<p>You now have details on every match in this database where Bologna won.</p>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="1.3.-CASE-with-Aggregation">1.3. <code>CASE</code> with Aggregation<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.3.-CASE-with-Aggregation">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong><code>CASE</code> with Aggregation Functions</strong>
-CASE WHEN with COUNT(): Count the rows.
-CASE WHEN with SUM(): Sum the values.
-CASE WHEN with AVG(): Average of values, or calculate percentage.</p>
<h4 id="1.3.1.-Example:-COUNT-using-CASE-WHEN">1.3.1. Example: <code>COUNT</code> using <code>CASE WHEN</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#1.3.1.-Example:-COUNT-using-CASE-WHEN">&#182;</a></h4><p>Do the number of soccer matches played in a given European country differ across seasons?</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[61]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    c.name AS country,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Count matches in each of the 3 seasons</span>
<span class="s2">    COUNT(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2012/2013&#39; THEN m.id END) AS matches_2012_2013,</span>
<span class="s2">    COUNT(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2013/2014&#39; THEN m.id END) AS matches_2013_2014,</span>
<span class="s2">    COUNT(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2014/2015&#39; THEN m.id END) AS matches_2014_2015</span>
<span class="s2">FROM country AS c</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">ON c.id = m.country_id</span>
<span class="s2">-- Group by country name alias</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY country;&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[61]:</div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<p>The number of matches played in each season seems relatively consistent across countries. Where do you see the largest difference?</p>
<h4 id="1.3.2.-Example:-SUM-and-CASE-WHEN-with-Multiple-Conditions">1.3.2. Example: <code>SUM</code> and <code>CASE WHEN</code> with Multiple Conditions<a class="anchor-link" href="#1.3.2.-Example:-SUM-and-CASE-WHEN-with-Multiple-Conditions">&#182;</a></h4><p>In Python, you have the ability to calculate a SUM of logical values (i.e., TRUE/FALSE) directly. In SQL, you have to convert these values into 1 and 0 before calculating a sum. This can be done using a CASE statement.</p>
<p>Your goal here is to use the country and match table to determine the total number of matches won by the home team in each country during the different seasons.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[62]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    c.name AS country,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Sum the total records in each season where the home team won</span>
<span class="s2">    SUM(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2012/2013&#39; AND m.home_team_goal &gt; m.away_team_goal </span>
<span class="s2">        THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS matches_2012_2013,</span>
<span class="s2">    SUM(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2013/2014&#39; AND m.home_team_goal &gt; m.away_team_goal </span>
<span class="s2">        THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS matches_2013_2014,</span>
<span class="s2">    SUM(CASE WHEN m.season = &#39;2014/2015&#39; AND m.home_team_goal &gt; m.away_team_goal </span>
<span class="s2">        THEN 1 ELSE 0 END) AS matches_2014_2015</span>
<span class="s2">FROM country AS c</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">ON c.id = m.country_id</span>
<span class="s2">-- Group by country name alias</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY country;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[62]:</div>

<h4 id="1.3.2.-Example:-Calculating-Percent-with-CASE-and-AVG">1.3.2. Example: Calculating Percent with <code>CASE</code> and <code>AVG</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#1.3.2.-Example:-Calculating-Percent-with-CASE-and-AVG">&#182;</a></h4><p>Examine the percentage of ties in each country in different seasons.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[63]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    c.name AS country,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Round the percentage of tied games to 2 decimal points</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Calculate the percentage of tied games in each season</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND(AVG(CASE WHEN m.season=&#39;2013/2014&#39; AND m.home_team_goal = m.away_team_goal THEN 1</span>
<span class="s2">             WHEN m.season=&#39;2013/2014&#39; AND m.home_team_goal != m.away_team_goal THEN 0</span>
<span class="s2">             END),2) AS pct_ties_2013_2014,</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND(AVG(CASE WHEN m.season=&#39;2014/2015&#39; AND m.home_team_goal = m.away_team_goal THEN 1</span>
<span class="s2">             WHEN m.season=&#39;2014/2015&#39; AND m.home_team_goal != m.away_team_goal THEN 0</span>
<span class="s2">             END),2) AS pct_ties_2014_2015</span>
<span class="s2">FROM country AS c</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">ON c.id = m.country_id</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY country;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h2 id="2.-Simple-Subquery">2. Simple Subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.-Simple-Subquery">&#182;</a></h2><p>Learn about subqueries in the <code>SELECT</code>, <code>FROM</code>, and <code>WHERE</code> clauses. You will gain an understanding of when subqueries are necessary to construct your dataset and where to best include them in your queries.</p>
<h3 id="2.1.-Subqueries-in-WHERE">2.1. Subqueries in <code>WHERE</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#2.1.-Subqueries-in-WHERE">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong>What is a Subquery?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>A query nested inside another query.</li>
<li>Useful for intermediary transformations.</li>
<li>Can be in any part of a query: SELECT, FROM, WHERE, GROUP BY.</li>
<li>Can return a variety of information<ul>
<li>Scalar quantities (Numbers).</li>
<li>A list used for filtering or joining.</li>
<li>A table to extract further transformation data.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong> Why Subqueries?</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Comparing groups to summarized values.<ul>
<li>Eg. How did Liverpool compare to the English Premier League’s average performance for that year?</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Reshaping data.<ul>
<li>Eg. What is the highest monthly average of goals scored in the Bundesliga?</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Combining data that cannot be joined.<ul>
<li>Eg. How do you get both the home and away team names into a table of match results?</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong> Subqueries in <code>WHERE</code></strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Used for filtering results.</li>
<li>Subquery can be evaluated independently from the outer query.</li>
<li>Is only processed once in the entire statement.</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="2.1.1.-Example:-Filtering-Using-Scalar-WHERE-Subqueries">2.1.1. Example: Filtering Using Scalar <code>WHERE</code> Subqueries<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.1.1.-Example:-Filtering-Using-Scalar-WHERE-Subqueries">&#182;</a></h4><p>Generate a list of matches where the total goals scored (for both teams in total) is more than 3 times the average for games in the 2013/2014 matches.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[64]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the date, home goals, and away goals scored</span>
<span class="s2">    date,</span>
<span class="s2">    home_team_goal,</span>
<span class="s2">    away_team_goal</span>
<span class="s2">FROM  match</span>
<span class="s2">-- Filter for matches where total goals exceeds 3x the average</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE season = &#39;2013/2014&#39; AND</span>
<span class="s2">      (home_team_goal + away_team_goal) &gt; </span>
<span class="s2">      (SELECT 3 * AVG(home_team_goal + away_team_goal)</span>
<span class="s2">        FROM match WHERE season = &#39;2013/2014&#39;); </span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[64]:</div>

<h4 id="2.1.2.-Example:-Filtering-Using-WHERE-Subqueries-with-a-List">2.1.2. Example: Filtering Using <code>WHERE</code> Subqueries with a List<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.1.2.-Example:-Filtering-Using-WHERE-Subqueries-with-a-List">&#182;</a></h4><p>Create a list of teams that scored 8 or more goals in a home match.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[65]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the team long and short names</span>
<span class="s2">    team_long_name,</span>
<span class="s2">    team_short_name</span>
<span class="s2">FROM team</span>
<span class="s2">-- Filter for teams with 8 or more home goals</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE team_api_id IN</span>
<span class="s2">      (SELECT home_team_api_id </span>
<span class="s2">       FROM match</span>
<span class="s2">       WHERE home_team_goal &gt;= 8);</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="2.2.-Subqueries-in-FROM">2.2. Subqueries in <code>FROM</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.-Subqueries-in-FROM">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong>Subqueries in <code>FROM</code></strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Restructure and transform your data<ul>
<li>Transforming data from long to wide before selecting</li>
<li>Prefiltering data</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Calculating aggregates of aggregates<ul>
<li>Eg. Which 3 teams has the highest average of home goals scored?</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>You can create multiple subqueries in one FROM statement<ul>
<li>Alias, and Join them!</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>You can join a subquery to a table in FROM<ul>
<li>Include a joining columns in both tables</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="2.2.1-Example:-Joining-Subqueries-in-FROM">2.2.1 Example: Joining Subqueries in <code>FROM</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#2.2.1-Example:-Joining-Subqueries-in-FROM">&#182;</a></h4><p>Generate a subquery using the match table, and then join that subquery to the country table to calculate information about matches with 10 or more goals in total.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[66]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select country name and the count match IDs</span>
<span class="s2">    c.name AS country_name,</span>
<span class="s2">    COUNT(sub.id) AS matches</span>
<span class="s2">FROM country AS c</span>
<span class="s2">-- Inner join the subquery onto country</span>
<span class="s2">-- Select the country id and match id columns</span>
<span class="s2">INNER JOIN (SELECT country_id, id </span>
<span class="s2">           FROM match</span>
<span class="s2">           -- Filter the subquery by matches with 10+ goals</span>
<span class="s2">           WHERE (home_team_goal + away_team_goal) &gt;= 10) AS sub</span>
<span class="s2">ON c.id = sub.country_id</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY country_name;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[66]:</div>

<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="2.3.-Subqueries-in-SELECT">2.3. Subqueries in <code>SELECT</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#2.3.-Subqueries-in-SELECT">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong>Subqueries in SELECT</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Returns a single value<ul>
<li>Include aggregate values to compare to individual values</li>
<li>Used in mathematical calculations</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Make sure you have all filters in the right places<ul>
<li>Properly filter both the main and the subquery!</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="2.3.1.-Example:-Subqueries-in-SELECT-for-Calculations">2.3.1. Example: Subqueries in <code>SELECT</code> for Calculations<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.3.1.-Example:-Subqueries-in-SELECT-for-Calculations">&#182;</a></h4><p>Create a column to compare each league's average total goals to the overall average goals in the 2013/2014 season. Also, add a column that directly compares these values by subtracting the overall average from the subquery.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[67]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the league name and average goals scored</span>
<span class="s2">    name AS league,</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND(AVG(m.home_team_goal + m.away_team_goal),2) AS avg_goals,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Subtract the overall average from the league average</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND(AVG(m.home_team_goal + m.away_team_goal) - </span>
<span class="s2">        (SELECT AVG(home_team_goal + away_team_goal)</span>
<span class="s2">         FROM match </span>
<span class="s2">         WHERE season = &#39;2013/2014&#39;),2) AS diff</span>
<span class="s2">FROM league AS l</span>
<span class="s2">LEFT JOIN match AS m</span>
<span class="s2">ON l.country_id = m.country_id</span>
<span class="s2">-- Only include 2013/2014 results</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE season = &#39;2013/2014&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">GROUP BY league</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY avg_goals DESC;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">

<p>Games in the Netherlands tend to score the highest number of goals on average in this season.</p>

</div>
</div>

<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="2.4.-Subqueries-Advice">2.4. Subqueries Advice<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.4.-Subqueries-Advice">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong> Must Know When Using Subqueries</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Can include multiple subqueries in SELECT, FROM, WHERE</li>
<li>Format your queries<ul>
<li>Line up SELECT, FROM, WHERE, and GROUP BY</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Annotate your queries<ul>
<li>Comment: /<em> ~ </em>/</li>
<li>In line Comment: -- ~</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Indent your queries<ul>
<li>CASE WHEN statement</li>
<li>Subqueries</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Properly filter each subquery</li>
<li>Is that subquery necessary?<ul>
<li>Subqueries require computing power</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="2.4.1.-Example:-Subqueries-Everywhere">2.4.1. Example: Subqueries Everywhere<a class="anchor-link" href="#2.4.1.-Example:-Subqueries-Everywhere">&#182;</a></h4><p>In soccer leagues, games are played at different stages. Winning teams progress from one stage to the next, until they reach the final stage. In each stage, the stakes become higher than the previous one.</p>
<p>Extract data examining the average goals scored in each stage of a match. Does the average number of goals scored change as the stakes get higher from one stage to the next?</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[69]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the stage and average goals from s</span>
<span class="s2">    stage,</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND(avg_goals,2) AS avg_goal,</span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the overall average for 2012/2013</span>
<span class="s2">    ROUND((SELECT AVG(home_team_goal + away_team_goal) FROM match WHERE season = &#39;2012/2013&#39;),2) AS overall_avg</span>
<span class="s2">FROM </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select the stage and average goals in 2012/2013 from match</span>
<span class="s2">    (SELECT</span>
<span class="s2">         stage,</span>
<span class="s2">         AVG(home_team_goal + away_team_goal) AS avg_goals</span>
<span class="s2">     FROM match</span>
<span class="s2">     WHERE season = &#39;2012/2013&#39;</span>
<span class="s2">     GROUP BY stage) AS s</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Filter the main query using the subquery</span>
<span class="s2">    s.avg_goals &gt; (SELECT AVG(home_team_goal + away_team_goal) </span>
<span class="s2">                    FROM match WHERE season = &#39;2012/2013&#39;)</span>
<span class="s2">ORDER BY stage DESC;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[69]:</div>

<h2 id="3.-Advanced-Subquery">3. Advanced Subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.-Advanced-Subquery">&#182;</a></h2><p>Learn how to use nested and correlated subqueries to extract more complex data from a relational database. You will also learn about common table expressions and how to best construct queries using multiple common table expressions.</p>
<h3 id="3.1.-Correlated-Subquery">3.1. Correlated Subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.-Correlated-Subquery">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong>Correlated Subquery</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Uses values from the outer query to generate a result.</li>
<li>Re-run for every row generated in the final data set.</li>
<li>Used for advanced joining, filtering, and evaluating data.</li>
</ul>
<table>
<thead><tr>
<th style="text-align:center">Simple Subquery</th>
<th style="text-align:center">Correlated Subquery</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">Can be run independently from the main query.</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Dependent on the main query to execute.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center">Evaluated once in the whole query.</td>
<td style="text-align:center">Evaluated in loops. Significantly slows down query run time.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h4 id="3.1.1-Example:-Basic-Correlated-Subquery">3.1.1 Example: Basic Correlated Subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.1.1-Example:-Basic-Correlated-Subquery">&#182;</a></h4><p>Practice using correlated subqueries to examine matches with scores that are extreme outliers for each country -- above 3 times the average score!</p>
<blockquote><p><strong>NOTE</strong>: The bottom query takes a while.</p>
</blockquote>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[70]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Select country ID, date, home, and away goals from match</span>
<span class="s2">    main.country_id,</span>
<span class="s2">    date,</span>
<span class="s2">    main.home_team_goal, </span>
<span class="s2">    main.away_team_goal</span>
<span class="s2">FROM match AS main</span>
<span class="s2">WHERE </span>
<span class="s2">    -- Filter the main query by the subquery</span>
<span class="s2">    (home_team_goal + away_team_goal) &gt; </span>
<span class="s2">        (SELECT AVG((sub.home_team_goal + sub.away_team_goal) * 3)</span>
<span class="s2">         FROM match AS sub</span>
<span class="s2">         -- Join the main query to the subquery in WHERE</span>
<span class="s2">         WHERE main.country_id = sub.country_id);</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output">

<p>Correlated subqueries take longer to produce results, but they often prevent you from having to create multiple subqueries.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing text_cell rendered"><div class="prompt input_prompt">
</div><div class="inner_cell">
<div class="text_cell_render border-box-sizing rendered_html">
<h3 id="3.2.-Nested-Subquery">3.2. Nested Subquery<a class="anchor-link" href="#3.2.-Nested-Subquery">&#182;</a></h3><p><strong> Nested Subquery</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Subquery inside another subquery.</li>
<li>Perform multiple layers of transformation.</li>
<li>Can be used with correlated subquery.</li>
</ul>
<h4 id="3.2.1.-Example:-Nest-a-Subquery-in-FROM">3.2.1. Example: Nest a Subquery in <code>FROM</code><a class="anchor-link" href="#3.2.1.-Example:-Nest-a-Subquery-in-FROM">&#182;</a></h4><p>What's the average number of matches per season where a team scored 5 or more goals? How does this differ by country?</p>
<p>Follwing is a nested subquery, that count the numbers of matches that score more than 5 in every seasons, for every country.</p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="cell border-box-sizing code_cell rendered">
<div class="input">
<div class="prompt input_prompt">In&nbsp;[71]:</div>
<div class="inner_cell">
    <div class="input_area">
<div class=" highlight hl-ipython3"><pre><span></span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;SELECT country_id, season,</span>
<span class="s2">         COUNT(id) AS matches</span>
<span class="s2">  FROM (</span>
<span class="s2">    SELECT country_id, season, id</span>
<span class="s2">    FROM match</span>
<span class="s2">    WHERE home_team_goal &gt;= 5 OR away_team_goal &gt;= 5) AS inner_s</span>
<span class="s2">  -- Close parentheses and alias the subquery</span>
<span class="s2">  GROUP BY country_id, season;</span>
<span class="s2">&quot;&quot;&quot;</span>
<span class="n">pd</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">read_sql</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">sql_stmt</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">conn</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">.</span><span class="n">head</span><span class="p">()</span>
</pre></div>

    </div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="output_wrapper">
<div class="output">


<div class="output_area">

    <div class="prompt output_prompt">Out[71]:</div>
